    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer16323127821619405659">From breathtaking stop-action animation to bittersweet modern fairy tales, filmmaker <b>Tim Burton</b> has become known for his unique visual brilliance – witty and macabre at once. Now he gives birth to a cast of gruesomely sympathetic children – misunderstood outcasts who struggle to find love and belonging in their cruel, cruel worlds.   <span id="freeText16323127821619405659" style="display:none">From breathtaking stop-action animation to bittersweet modern fairy tales, filmmaker <b>Tim Burton</b> has become known for his unique visual brilliance – witty and macabre at once. Now he gives birth to a cast of gruesomely sympathetic children – misunderstood outcasts who struggle to find love and belonging in their cruel, cruel worlds. His lovingly lurid illustrations evoke both the sweetness and the tragedy of these dark yet simple beings – hopeful, hapless heroes who appeal to the ugly outsider in all of us, and let us laugh at a world we have long left behind (mostly anyway).</span>

<div id="review_691821898" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/691821898" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16458477-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606198430p2/16458477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/691821898?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/16458477-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571224449" href="/book/show/945817.The_Melancholy_Death_of_Oyster_Boy_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16458477-tina?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer691821898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17225113379679143654">This is me--a huge Tim Burton fan (or so I thought):<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383547153i/6592492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>One day, while carelessly browsing the Internets, I came across a book that I had no idea existed. I couldn't believe my eyes and felt especially stupid when realization hit me: I must have been living under a rock in a God-forsaken place, as never before had I heard of this book:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432631i/869168.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Of course, as soon as I realized that I had to have this book, another realization hit bullseye: remember that God-forsaken place, the one where I lived under a rock? </span>
  <span id="freeText17225113379679143654" style="display:none">This is me--a huge Tim Burton fan (or so I thought):<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383547153i/6592492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One day, while carelessly browsing the Internets, I came across a book that I had no idea existed. I couldn't believe my eyes and felt especially stupid when realization hit me: I must have been living under a rock in a God-forsaken place, as never before had I heard of this book:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432631i/869168.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, as soon as I realized that I had to have this book, another realization hit bullseye: remember that God-forsaken place, the one where I lived under a rock? Yes, this book is not available anywhere in Bulgaria. This is where frustration got the better of me...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432631i/869169.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But I said to myself: "Fear not, Tina, for you have the power of the Internets and the credit card, and have been given upon birth the gift of patience--you shall order this book online from a country where Tim Burton's books actually exist!". <br><br>This is me now, loving my book and loving Tim Burton even more:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432631i/869170._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17225113379679143654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425442669?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9789649694331" href="/book/show/2040078._">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer8487675249917636153">The melancholy death of Oyster Boy & other stories, Timothy Walter Burton<br/><br/>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy & Other Stories is a 1997 poetry book written and illustrated by American film director Timothy Walter Burton. <br/><br/>The poems, which are full of black humor, tell stories of hybrid kids, spontaneous transformers, and women who have babies to win over men.<br/><br/>Some characters of the book would later appear in the Flash series Stainboy, which was created, directed, and written by Burton: Stick Boy and</span>
  <span id="freeText8487675249917636153" style="display:none">The melancholy death of Oyster Boy &amp; other stories, Timothy Walter Burton<br /><br />The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy &amp; Other Stories is a 1997 poetry book written and illustrated by American film director Timothy Walter Burton. <br /><br />The poems, which are full of black humor, tell stories of hybrid kids, spontaneous transformers, and women who have babies to win over men.<br /><br />Some characters of the book would later appear in the Flash series Stainboy, which was created, directed, and written by Burton: Stick Boy and Match Girl in Love, Voodoo Girl, Robot Boy, Staring Girl, The Boy with Nails in His Eyes, The Girl with Many Eyes, Stain Boy, The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy, Stain Boy's Special Christmas, The Girl Who Turned into a Bed, Roy the Toxic Boy, James, Stick Boy's Festive Season, Brie Boy, Mummy Boy, Junk Girl, The Pin Cushion Queen, Melon head, Sue, Jimmy the Hideous Penguin Boy, Char Boy, Anchor Baby, Oyster Boy Steps Out.<br /><br />عنوانها: مرگ غم‌ انگیز پسر صدفی و قصه‌ های دیگر؛ مرگ وحشتناک پسرک صدفی و داستان‌های دیگر؛ اثر: تیم برتون؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش روز پانزدهم ماه می سال 2009 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: مرگ غم‌ انگیز پسر صدفی و قصه‌ های دیگر؛ اثر: تیم برتون؛ برگردان احسان نوروزی؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، حرفه‌ هنرمند، 1388، مشخصات ظاهری 127ص، مصور ( بخشی رنگی )‏‫؛ 14×19س‌م.‬، شابک 9649694331؛ مجموعه داستانهای خیلی کوتاه با سوژه های عجیب معصومیت و وحشت از نویسندگان و کارگردانان امریکایی؛ - سده 20م<br /><br />با عنوان: مرگ وحشتناک پسرک صدفی و داستان‌های دیگر؛ در سال 1384هجری خورشیدی، توسط نشر زاوش، نیز منتشر شده است<br /><br />مرگ غم‌انگیز پسر صدفی، و قصه‌های دیگر؛ عنوان کتاب شعر مصوری است، که توسط «تیم برتون (خالق فیلمهای بتمن)»، نگاشته و تصویرگری شد، و نخستین بار در سال 1997میلادی انتشار یافته است؛ کتاب پر از اشعاری با درون‌مایه ی کمدی سیاه است، و داستان موجودات عجیب و غریبی را بیان می‌کند؛ برخی از شخصیت‌های این کتاب، بعدها در مجموعه ی کوتاه انیمیشنی، به کارگردانی «تیم برتون» به کار گرفته شدند؛ «ادوارد دست قیچی»، «عروس مرده»، «کابوس قبل از کریسمس» و «ماهی بزرگ»، نمونه ای از بچه های هولناک، و دوست داشتنی در این کتاب هستند؛ مطرودین تنهایی که میکوشند عشق را بیابند، و به دنیاهای بیرحم ستمکاراشان وابستگی پیدا کنند؛ تصویرسازیهای دوست داشتنی «تیم برتون»، همزمان شادی و تراژدی این موجودات پر امید اما تیره بخت را هویدا و آشکار میسازند<br /><br /><b>مرگ غم انگیز پسر صدفی (قصه ای از تیم برتون)؛</b><br />در تپه های شنی خواستگاری کرد؛<br />در کنار دریا ازدواج کردند<br />ماه عسل نه روزه شان در جزیره ی کاپری بود.؛<br /><br />برای شام غذای خاصی داشتند<br />خورشت جاافتاده ی نرمتنان با ماهی.؛<br /><br />وقتی مرد آب خورش را مزه مزه میکرد؛<br />عروس خانم در دل آرزویی کرد.؛<br /><br />آن آرزو برآورده شد - بچه به دنیا آمد<br />یک چنین چیز کوچکی آدمیزاد بود؟<br />خب، شاید.؛<br /><br />ده تا انگشت دست، ده تا انگشت پا، دل و روده و قوه ی بینایی.؛<br />میتوانست بشنود، میتوانست حس کند؛<br />ولی آیا معمولی بود؟<br /><br />نه چندان.؛<br />این تولد غیرطبیعی، این مصیبت، این آفت؛<br />غم اول و آخر این زن و شوهر بود.؛<br /><br />زن به دکتر شکایت کرد: «این بچه نمیتونه مال من باشه؛<br />بوی اقیانوس میده، بوی خزه و آب دریا»؛<br /><br />تازه شما خیلی هم خوش شانسید، همین هفته ی پیش؛ دختری رو درمان کردم که سه تا چشم داشت و یک منقار<br />اینکه پسرتون نصفش صدفه، تقصیر من نیست؛<br />برحسب اتفاق متوجه نشدین که ...؛<br />یه خونه ی کوچیک کنار دریا هست؟؛<br /><br />زن و مرد نمیدانستند چه اسمی برایش بگذارند<br />سام صداش زدن؛<br />یا بعضی وقتها هم بهش میگفتن: «همون چیزی که شبیه صدفه»؛<br /><br />همه منتظر بودند ولی هیچکس نمیتوانست پیش بینی کند<br />پسر صدفیِ جوان چه وقت از صدفش بیرون میآید<br /><br />وقتی یکروز چشم چهارقلوهای تامسن بهش افتاد<br />بهش گفتند جانور صدفی و زود در رفتند<br /><br />یک بعد از ظهر بهاری<br />سام زیر باران ماند<br /><br />گوشه ای در جنوب غربی سی ویو و مِین<br />نشست به تماشای آب باران که چرخ میخورد و<br />میریخت تو جوب.؛<br /><br />مادرش تو بزرگراه<br />زده بود بغل<br />و داشت میکوفت روی داشبورد ماشین<br />طاقت نداشت<br />این غم<br />نا امیدی<br />و رنج بی انتها را<br /><br />مادر گفت: آره عزیز دلم، نمیخوام دستت بندازم، ولی یه چیزی بدجور بوی ماهی میده، فکر کنم بوی پسرته<br /><br />دوست ندارم این رو بگم، ولی بالاخره باید گفت دیگه، تو مشکلات رو میندازی تقصیر پسرمون<br /><br />مرد مرهمها را امتحان کرد، روغنهایی که<br />همه چیز را به رنگ قرمز درمیآوردند<br />معجون و کرمهای مختلف<br />و شربت سرب را امتحان کرد<br />درد کشید و همه جایش خارید و لرزید و خون آمد<br /><br />دکتر اینطور تشخیص داد: «نمیتونم مطمئن باشم، ولی شاید علت مرض، درمانش هم باشه، میگن صدف قدرتت رو زیاد میکنه، شاید خوردن پسرت، تو این قضایا کمکت کنه!»؛<br /><br />مرد پاورچین آمد، یواشکی، خیس عرق<br />و بر لب هایش-دروغ محض<br /><br />؛«پسرم،تو خوشبختی؟ نمیخوام فضولی کنم، ولی تو خواب بهشت نمیبینی؟<br />هیچ وقت دلت نخواسته بمیری؟»؛<br /><br />سام دوبار پلک زد<br />ولی جوابی نداد<br /><br />پدر به چاقویش دست کشید و کراواتش را شل کرد<br />وقتی پسرش را بلند میکرد، سام کت پدر را خیس کرد<br />پدر صدف را برد کنار لبهایش<br />و سام را قورت داد پایین<br /><br />پسر را در شنهای ساحل خاک کردند<br />دعا کردند و اشک ریختند<br />ساعت سه رسیدند خانه<br /><br />یک صلیب از چوب شناور خاکستری، نشانه ی قبر پسر صدفی شد<br /><br />روی شنها نوشته بود<br />خدا بیامرزدش<br /><br />خاطره ی پسر صدفی با موجی بلند پاک شد و رفت<br /><br />در فضای امن خانه<br />مرد به زنش گفت: «از خدا بچه ای دیگر طلب کنیم»؛<br />زن زمزمه کرد: «ولی اینبار آرزوی دختر کنیم»؛ تیم برتون<br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2735261206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2735261206" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735261206?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571345106" href="/book/show/37859262-the-melancholy-death-of-oyster-boy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=american-literature">american-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=gothic-fiction">gothic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735261206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14006045224713454241"><i>
  <b>‘’The final gasp of his short life<br/>Was sickly with despair.<br/>Whoever thought that you could die<br/>From breathing outdoor air?’’</b>
</i><br/><br/>For most lovers of the 7th Art, Tim Burton is an incredible talent. For us Gothic aficionados, Tim Burton is a genius, a pioneer whose creations opened the audience's heart and mind to the contemporary Gothic style, aesthetics, and philosophy. He is the one who found the perfect balance between the satire of how most people perceive the Gothic wave, evident in <i>Beetlejuice</i>,</span>
  <span id="freeText14006045224713454241" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘’The final gasp of his short life<br />Was sickly with despair.<br />Whoever thought that you could die<br />From breathing outdoor air?’’</b>
</i><br /><br />For most lovers of the 7th Art, Tim Burton is an incredible talent. For us Gothic aficionados, Tim Burton is a genius, a pioneer whose creations opened the audience's heart and mind to the contemporary Gothic style, aesthetics, and philosophy. He is the one who found the perfect balance between the satire of how most people perceive the Gothic wave, evident in <i>Beetlejuice</i>, and the sadness, isolation and blind persecution of the Different, the Other exceptionally depicted in his masterpiece <i>Edward Scissorhands</i>. The majority of his films is a hymn to the feelings of those who are isolated by a society that cannot understand or accept. <i>Corpse Bride</i>, <i>Big Eyes</i>, <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, the violent, captivating <i>Sweeney Todd</i>, the exceptional <i>Alice In Wonderland</i>, the atmospheric <i>Sleepy Hollow</i> and his contribution to the classic <i>The Nightmare Before Christmas</i>.<br /><br />The 20th-anniversary edition of <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy</i> is a collection of poems dedicated to characters that would find themselves in the company of Edward Scissorhands. Little ones in all their sweet ‘’ugliness’’ and weirdness. Sadness, loneliness, children denied by their parents. The Stick Boy, the Staring Girl, the Robot Boy and the Boy With Nails in His Eyes. The Stain Boy, the Voodoo Girl, the Toxic Boy, and the Mummy Boy and the unfortunate Oyster Boy of the title. Poems that may appear funny on the surface but hide a deep bitterness for choices that are not made by the unfortunate souls whose course leads to dark places. Beautiful, gothic and whimsical sketches, clever rhymes full of black humor and bitter truths.<br /><br />I don’t think we expected anything less by Tim Burton, a true genius…<br /><br /> <i>
  <b>‘’You should count yourself lucky, for only last week,<br />I treated a girl with three eyes and beak.<br />That your son is half oyster<br />You cannot blame me.<br />....have you considered, by chance,<br />A small home by the sea?’’</b>
</i><br /><br />My reviews can also be found on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theopinionatedreaderblog.wordpress.com">https://theopinionatedreaderblog.word...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14006045224713454241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1868249685" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868249685" />
    <a title="Kenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1642452-kenny"><img alt="Kenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472073986p2/1642452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1868249685?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenny" href="/user/show/1642452-kenny">Kenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=short-stories-novellas">short-stories-novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1642452-kenny?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1868249685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13587991601744696611"><b><i>“Alone and rejected, Mummy Boy wept,<br/>then went to the cabinet<br/>where the snack food was kept.”</i> <br/>― Tim Burton, The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556662912i/27436905._SX540_.jpg' alt='1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I needed to read today. I didn't want to simply read, <b>
  <u>I NEEDED to read</u>
</b>. I felt a need to clear the voices of Mrs. Dalloway from my mind. <b>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</b>, was the perfect book to do so. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483762746i/21646903._SX540_.jpg' alt='1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>This is a collection of grim short poems/stories depicting the lives and misfortunes of a group of sympathetic outc</span>
  <span id="freeText13587991601744696611" style="display:none"><b><i>“Alone and rejected, Mummy Boy wept,<br>then went to the cabinet<br>where the snack food was kept.”</i> <br>― Tim Burton, The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556662912i/27436905._SX540_.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I needed to read today. I didn't want to simply read, <b>
  <u>I NEEDED to read</u>
</b>. I felt a need to clear the voices of Mrs. Dalloway from my mind. <b>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</b>, was the perfect book to do so. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483762746i/21646903._SX540_.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This is a collection of grim short poems/stories depicting the lives and misfortunes of a group of sympathetic outcasts as they try to find their place in the world -- often with tragic results.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483762746i/21646904.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A stick boy finds himself engulfed in flames when he falls in love with the wrong kind of girl, a voodoo doll is cursed to be forever alone because of the pins sticking out from her heart, a depressed melonhead discovers he should be careful with what he wishes for, and Roy, known as ‘toxic boy’, learns he cannot coexist with fresh, clean air.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426673635i/14077534._SX540_.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Angst and a sense of ‘not really belonging here’ are a given throughout the poems in an homage to adolescence, and even though the content of some of them is quite dark it is difficult not to empathize with the protagonists.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483762746i/21646905.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy &amp; Other Stories is macabre, disturbing, funny and heartwarming all at the same time. It’s Tim Burton. It's the perfect opportunity to visit Burton’s unique and unusual mind, and is not to be missed.</span>

<div id="review_739472427" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739472427" />
    <a title="Florencia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21575078-florencia"><img alt="Florencia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601866797p2/21575078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/739472427?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Florencia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Florencia" href="/user/show/21575078-florencia">Florencia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">burton fans, dark humor lovers.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Florencia by: </span>
      me!
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21575078-florencia?shelf=stories-and-novellas-for-this-life">stories-and-novellas-for-this-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21575078-florencia?shelf=funny-and-ish">funny-and-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21575078-florencia?shelf=graphic-novels-weird-comics">graphic-novels-weird-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739472427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10201031100840892485">I'm a fan of Burton's movies. So I was kind of interested in his writings. It wasn't a big surprise to find out that the level of awesome weirdness was similar. The distinctive Burton mixture of darkness and uncomfortable tenderness. <br/><br/>I mean, he wrote some really odd poems (technically, not that great, and that is a charming plus) but their sweetness and sensibility are touching. Well, most of the times, they're just sad. However, this book is written in a way that seems to be funny, and for some</span>
  <span id="freeText10201031100840892485" style="display:none">I'm a fan of Burton's movies. So I was kind of interested in his writings. It wasn't a big surprise to find out that the level of awesome weirdness was similar. The distinctive Burton mixture of darkness and uncomfortable tenderness. <br><br>I mean, he wrote some really odd poems (technically, not that great, and that is a charming plus) but their sweetness and sensibility are touching. Well, most of the times, they're just sad. However, this book is written in a way that seems to be funny, and for some people, it includes some weird poems which made them laugh and that's it. But after a while, its melancholic humor kicks in, and you just feel bad for most of the characters, many of them rather relatable. I wanted to help them, to adopt them and bring them home and have picnics everyday and dance under a rainbow and clean the house while a couple of birds make their beds. Nevertheless, this is the Burton universe. From a certain perspective, it's not that different from the real world.<br><br>Besides the poems, Burton also drew some lovely cartoons (hardly appropriate for children). If you're going to read about a boy with nails in his eyes, it's nice to see a detailed picture of it, right? <br>Same thing with a girl with many eyes. <br>Imagine the flood she'd cause if you ever make her cry. <br><br>There are poems like <i>The Girl Who Turned into a Bed</i>, <i>Sue</i> and <i>Jimmy, the Hideous Penguin Boy</i> which made me smile as my mind repeated "what a piece of rare work this guy is". Others like <i>The Melancholy death of Oyster Boy</i> almost made me cry. <i>Voodoo girl</i> is funny poem with a heartbreaking ending line. <i>Anchor baby</i>, simply tragic. Oh, <i>Melonhead</i>! You have to read this good advice.<br><blockquote>
<b>Melonhead</b><br>There once was a morose melonhead,<br>who sat there all day<br>and wished he were dead.</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382817562i/6221321._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>But you should be careful<br>about the things that you wish.<br>Because the last thing he heard<br>was a deafening squish.</blockquote><br><br>Rare and isolated creatures, kids who don't fit normal standards and are rejected by their parents and laughed at by their neighbors, eccentric people with strange problems. This book is about all the weirdos that are far more interesting than the apparently regular, normal people - a girl with only two eyes, for instance. <br>This collection, beautifully illustrated, is a gem. It's one of those books which seems ostensibly simple but contains complex ideas, forgotten values and relatable feelings.<br><br><br>Oct 26, 13<br>* Also on <a href="https://nonbookreviews.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a>.<br>* Photo credit: Picture from <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10201031100840892485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=disturbing">disturbing</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872547664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5220616488173596090">Reading this tiny tome was sort of like taking a prolonged vacation on The Island of Really, Really Misfit Toys. The natives are strange but friendly. They take some getting used to, but after a while, you'll want to hug them...BUT be careful - many of them have sharp objects sticking out of their bellies.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394029421i/8798091.jpg' width='293' height='388' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>The Boy with Nails in His Eyes<br/><br/>The Boy with Nails in His Eyes<br/>put up his aluminum tree.<br/>It looked pretty strange<br/>because he couldn't see.</i>
</b><br/><br/>The above is a pretty good example of what's in this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText5220616488173596090" style="display:none">Reading this tiny tome was sort of like taking a prolonged vacation on The Island of Really, Really Misfit Toys. The natives are strange but friendly. They take some getting used to, but after a while, you'll want to hug them...BUT be careful - many of them have sharp objects sticking out of their bellies.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394029421i/8798091.jpg" width="293" height="388" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>The Boy with Nails in His Eyes<br><br>The Boy with Nails in His Eyes<br>put up his aluminum tree.<br>It looked pretty strange<br>because he couldn't see.</i>
</b><br><br>The above is a pretty good example of what's in this book and should tell you whether or not it's for you. Bad things happen to stick figures and little mummy boys. Children get eaten by their parents and a girl turns into a bed.<br><br>If you have a fondness for all things misbegotten AND find that fairy tales are not quite disturbing enough, you should have room in your heart for Melonhead and maybe even Jimmy, the Hideous Penguin Boy.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/638631854?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecily" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily">Cecily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571224449" href="/book/show/945817.The_Melancholy_Death_of_Oyster_Boy_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=humour">humour</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer638631854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2164797424007562494">A short collection of macabre poems, illustrated like a children's book, but aimed more at the YA market, and delightful for dark-thinking adults as well. <br/><br/>There are lots of gory things about eyes, stories of non-human children (toxic, half robot, half oyster etc) and a most inappropriate present from Santa. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508003115i/24174072._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Occasionally the rhythm doesn't quite work at the first attempt, but even so, it's great fun. <br/><br/>It is strongly reminiscent of <b>Hilaire Belloc's Cautionary Tales for Children</b> (my review <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47045092' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a>), bu</span>
  <span id="freeText2164797424007562494" style="display:none">A short collection of macabre poems, illustrated like a children's book, but aimed more at the YA market, and delightful for dark-thinking adults as well. <br><br>There are lots of gory things about eyes, stories of non-human children (toxic, half robot, half oyster etc) and a most inappropriate present from Santa. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508003115i/24174072._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Occasionally the rhythm doesn't quite work at the first attempt, but even so, it's great fun. <br><br>It is strongly reminiscent of <b>Hilaire Belloc's Cautionary Tales for Children</b> (my review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47045092" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>), but VERY obviously the work of Tim Burton. His wiry, but colour, illustrations, perfectly complement his dark words.</span>

<div id="review_1636817384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1636817384" />
    <a title="Asghar Abbas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37421322-asghar-abbas"><img alt="Asghar Abbas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444319622p2/37421322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1636817384?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asghar Abbas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asghar Abbas" href="/user/show/37421322-asghar-abbas">Asghar Abbas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571224449" href="/book/show/945817.The_Melancholy_Death_of_Oyster_Boy_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1636817384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3163682639177481340"><br/>I wonder what it would be like to live inside Tim Burton's head ala Being John Malkovich, such talent, such virile imaginations, to dwell within his noggin for a while, you know? I don't know why but for some reason I have always held Burton's creativity on par with Neil Gaiman's, though their style is very dissimilar, but both have distinct styles, that's almost as important as talent. I feel these little stories about grotesque beauty, and what a beauty it was, were full of metaphors, heavy wi</span>
  <span id="freeText3163682639177481340" style="display:none"><br />I wonder what it would be like to live inside Tim Burton's head ala Being John Malkovich, such talent, such virile imaginations, to dwell within his noggin for a while, you know? I don't know why but for some reason I have always held Burton's creativity on par with Neil Gaiman's, though their style is very dissimilar, but both have distinct styles, that's almost as important as talent. I feel these little stories about grotesque beauty, and what a beauty it was, were full of metaphors, heavy with symbolism. Too many hidden meanings here to be casual, Burton was trying to tell us something. In so few words and splashes from his mind, he did rather well. I went into this fully expecting weird quirkiness, maybe little bit of creepy Gothicness, but I found most of the stories to be very twisted darkly so, which I end up enjoying anyways. There was a lot of sexual innuendo, more so than in his films, that did surprise me. But I like it when I am surprised. <br /><br />OK, so let's break it down, shall we? Stick Boy and Match Girl were very sweet but in a Tim Burton fashion. Staring Girl was downright creepy, brrr. Stain Boy and his power were hilarious. OK now, the titular Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy, Jesus that was something else, quite an impact. Wow. It was definitely multilayered, with myriad themes and that ending, it's all about the endings, isn't it Rðhisha? It had a good beginning with these words ( he proposed in the dunes, they wed by the sea) and a good, righteous end. Stain Boy again, haha. The Girl Who Turned into a Bed, well! Roy the Toxic Boy, how ironic. James, my personal favorite but made me said Whattt aloud. Mummy Boy was like a twisted WALL-E. But my absolute favorite was the Anchor Baby because mermaids and watery stuff, it was so poignant and it had a proper satisfying finish, it was fair like chaos, this was definitely a social commentary. Junk Girl was very meaningful. All these stories strange but good. <br /><br />Tim Burton's stories have always been about the lonely hearts, the misfits, about isolation. Those who shun the world and are often rejected by it. Those distorted monsters, my heroes. I think all his work is basically a retelling of Frankenstein's monster and the need to separate from others' reality, about the misunderstood. I feel like he's trying to find a cure for the sickness of being alive and assuage the hysteria of living in this world. I have always cherished his movies, but his vision transcends even here to the written form as well. I feel like I know him a little better for it, after reading this collection. <br /><br />Is it devious of me to enjoy all this weird craziness and all this misery? But it's so beautiful, she's so beautiful. Do you know you are fake? In the end, all I can say is this. Don't forget the music, don't forget the magic. Don't let utterly Empty People take all that away from you. <br /><br />Dream. Dream it all. Dream until you fall asleep. Dream till they let you. Even then dream some more, just to spite them, just for the heck of it. There's no Alice's sister here to wake you up. Don't be afraid, be a Dreamer even if there is no Eva Green.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3163682639177481340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_159343437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159343437" />
    <a title="Aldrin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160532-aldrin"><img alt="Aldrin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237990392p2/2160532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159343437?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aldrin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aldrin" href="/user/show/2160532-aldrin">Aldrin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780571195121" href="/book/show/18743.The_Melancholy_Death_Of_Oyster_Boy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159343437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10912602977444721820">Half-oyster, half-boy, Oyster Boy is born to a perfectly human couple who supposedly conceived him after dining on “one spectatular dish- / a simmering stew of mollusks and fish.” Growing up, Oyster Boy, whose proper name is Sam but is sometimes called "that thing that looks like a clam," becomes a laughingstock (“When the Thompson quadruplets espied him one day, / they called him a bivalve and ran quickly away.) and a picture of sadness and reticence (“One spring afternoon, / Sam was left in th</span>
  <span id="freeText10912602977444721820" style="display:none">Half-oyster, half-boy, Oyster Boy is born to a perfectly human couple who supposedly conceived him after dining on “one spectatular dish- / a simmering stew of mollusks and fish.” Growing up, Oyster Boy, whose proper name is Sam but is sometimes called "that thing that looks like a clam," becomes a laughingstock (“When the Thompson quadruplets espied him one day, / they called him a bivalve and ran quickly away.) and a picture of sadness and reticence (“One spring afternoon, / Sam was left in the rain. / At the southwestern corner of Seaview and Main, / he watched the rain water as it swirled / down the drain.”). Meanwhile his parents, unmindful of their offspring’s existential crisis, are having some problems of their own--specifically, problems in bed. Recall the long-standing reputation of oysters as powerful aphrodisiacs and you get a clue as to where Oyster Boy’s story is probably headed. Indeed, the circumstances surrounding the untimely demise of Oyster Boy, one of the many bizarre characters in <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy &amp; Other Stories</i>, is nothing if not melancholy. <br /><br /><i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy &amp; Other Stories</i> is a collection of poems written by filmmaker Tim Burton. The poems, all 23 of them, are about an unlikely assortment of extraordinary children. Products as they are of the warped imagination of the famous director of <i>Edward Scissorhands</i>, <i>Corpse Bride</i>, <i>Sweeney Todd</i>, and nearly everything else Johnny Depp starred in as an oddball, they are extraordinary not because they possess above-average strength and intelligence but because they have freakish appearances and sorrowful encounters with fate. <br /><br />A sampling of the titles in this collection yields funny-until-you-realize-they're-not eponymous characters, like The Boy with Nails in His Eyes, The Girl Who Turned Into a Bed, and Melonhead. Mummy Boy, “the result of an old pharoah's curse," and Robot Boy, apparently the consequence of a married woman’s affair with a microwave blender, share with Oyster Boy not only the same gender (obviously) but also the same unenviable feeling of being rejected and neglected, especially by their parents. <br /><br />The twenty odd characters in this book (Oyster Boy and two other characters appear twice) are children who inspire sympathy not so much for their grotesque abnormalities as for the simple ways they get to accept and cope with them. Often their stories end in tragedy, which is how things turn out for Oyster Boy and Roy, The Toxic Boy, but in some cases these strange fellows appear to think, "To heck with it!" The cape-wearing Stain Boy, who "can't fly around tall buildings, / or outrun a speeding train, / the only talent he seems to have / is to leave a nasty stain," is coolly unconcerned of his "sky-high" dry cleaning bill. The Pin Cushion Queen ("When she sits alone on her throne / pins push through her spleen.") sits alone on her throne anyway. <br /><br />Aside from composing the lines that narrate their not so kid-friendly stories, Burton also illustrated the plight of Oyster Boy and his miserable company in this collection. Already in the first drawing, of <i>The Nightmare Before Christmas</i>’ Jack Skellington lookalike Stick Boy and the endearing yet deathly Match Girl, the clearly mismatched young lovers in the first story, shades of Burton’s filmography and strokes guided by his fascination with the great Edward Gorey are at mischievous work. His illustrations add to the dark humor of his playful poems as well as to the intrinsic humanity of his characters, freaks and geeks who are actually--if you'll permit the poor rhyme--beautiful creatures in spite of their ugly features. <br /><br />Now why does that description sound awfully familiar?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10912602977444721820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5675811921000305593" style="display:none">I love Tim Burton's movies for their beautiful cinematography and sense of macabre with a pinch of dark humor. <br>His poetry is right up my alley, just like the stories of Edward Gorey (who is known to have influenced Burton). <br><br><b>Roy, the Toxic Boy</b><br><br><i>To those who knew him<br>-his friends-<br>we called him Roy.<br>To others he was known<br>as that horrible Toxic Boy.<br><br>He loved ammonia and asbestos,<br>and lots of cigarette smoke.<br>What he breathed in for air<br>would make other people choke!<br><br>His very favorite toy<br>was a can of aerosol spray;<br>he'd sit quietly and shake it,<br>and spray it all the day.<br><br>He'd stand inside the garage<br>in the early-morning frost,<br>waiting for the car to start<br>and fill him with exhaust.<br><br>The one and only time<br>I ever saw Toxic Boy cry<br>was when some sodium chloride<br>got into his eye.<br><br>One day for fresh air<br>they put him in the garden.<br>His face went deathly pale<br>and his body began to harden.<br><br>The final gasp of his short life<br>was sickly with despair.<br>Whoever thought that you could die<br>from breathing outdoor air?<br><br>As Roy's soul left his body<br>we all said a silent prayer.<br>It drifted up to heaven<br>and left a hole in the ozone layer.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417663i/826353._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How awesomely weird is that?<br><br>You can read the book here (it seems to be complete):<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://homepage.tinet.ie/~sebulbac/burton/home.html">http://homepage.tinet.ie/~sebulbac/bu...</a></span>

<div id="review_1046046093" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1046046093" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1046046093?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571224449" href="/book/show/945817.The_Melancholy_Death_of_Oyster_Boy_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1046046093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17808623960775034918">This is a collection of very very short stories which are all written in verse and have an accompanying illustration or illustrations. This whole book was written and illustrated by Tim Burton who is one of my favourite artists and I was very intrigued when I stumbled across this on Amazon. It's a very small book but it's a brilliant one and I have to say that it was better than I thought it would be.<br/><br/>This collection showcases some of Burton's weird character ideas and stories and whilst some sto</span>
  <span id="freeText17808623960775034918" style="display:none">This is a collection of very very short stories which are all written in verse and have an accompanying illustration or illustrations. This whole book was written and illustrated by Tim Burton who is one of my favourite artists and I was very intrigued when I stumbled across this on Amazon. It's a very small book but it's a brilliant one and I have to say that it was better than I thought it would be.<br /><br />This collection showcases some of Burton's weird character ideas and stories and whilst some stories (such as the Oyster Boy one) span a couple of pages in wonderful verse and with a sad and woeful tale, others are purely a line or two with the illustration to make you think and wonder. None of these stories were cheery, they all have a melancholy sadness or loneliness about them and each of the peculiar creations are misunderstood and isolated. However, the stories are wonderful and funny and entertaining to read and the illustrations just make this book a wonderful one to add to your collection.<br /><br />Although this looks like a children's book in design (verse + pictures usually = kids book) it's certainly got some more disturbing characters and the stories are all somewhat tragic and chaotic. I wouldn't, therefore, recommend this as a book to give to or read to kids, but I would say that the ironic beauty of these stories is certainly worth a go and I loved reading through this book.<br /><br />I also feel like this book has great re-readability to it and I have no doubt that I will pick this up again someday to re-read and re-experience these sad little tales. Highly recommended! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17808623960775034918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_13167985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13167985" />
    <a title="Robert Beveridge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/766524-robert-beveridge"><img alt="Robert Beveridge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286387835p2/766524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/13167985?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Beveridge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Beveridge" href="/user/show/766524-robert-beveridge">Robert Beveridge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=finished">finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=cle-pub-lib">cle-pub-lib</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13167985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17227701486799032745">Tim Burton, The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories (Morrow, 1997)<br/><br/>Someone needs to explain this to me and fast, `cause I don't get it: how is it that bad poetry (and yes, folks, this is truly bad) and art that looks like a second-rate Edward Gorey ripoff (Burton is not the illustrator that he is the sculptor and animator) can be so insanely funny? I am completely at a loss for why I liked this anywhere near as much as I did.<br/><br/>Let's face it, if you squint right while watching The Night</span>
  <span id="freeText17227701486799032745" style="display:none">Tim Burton, The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories (Morrow, 1997)<br /><br />Someone needs to explain this to me and fast, `cause I don't get it: how is it that bad poetry (and yes, folks, this is truly bad) and art that looks like a second-rate Edward Gorey ripoff (Burton is not the illustrator that he is the sculptor and animator) can be so insanely funny? I am completely at a loss for why I liked this anywhere near as much as I did.<br /><br />Let's face it, if you squint right while watching The Nightmare Before Christmas, it's obvious even in Burton's finest work that the specter of Edward Gorey looms large over Burton's material; it has never been more obvious than it is here. Many of his characters even seem to have the same basic brushstrokes Gorey used in his illustrations. Which is not to say they're bad; they just look like Edward Gorey work. Not even as blurred as Bacon's famous study of Pope Pius.<br /><br />And the verse? Absolute doggerel. Even conceding the idea that Burton is using Gerard Manley Hopkins-esque sprung rhythm (which he's not, because sprung rhythm does, at least, HAVE a rhythm), the implementation is so amateurish that it's impossible despite the rhymes to call this anything resembling poetry.<br /><br />but good living Christ on a crutch, is this book funny. Morbid, twisted, insane, gut-churning (despite the pretty cartoons, folks, this is not one to buy for the kiddies; flip through the title story for a good example of why), and full of laughs. One almost gets the idea Burton was going for a place as the anti-Dr. Seuss. Little vignettes about characters who fade in and out like Dish Network reception in a typhoon, popping up unexpectedly here and there and doing exactly what you were hoping they wouldn't.<br /><br />If you are at all a fan of Tim Burton, this is a must-read. If you're not, you're probably going to notice the faults and not find what lies beneath them. *** </span>
  <a data-text-id="17227701486799032745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3365016740?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CG" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CG" href="/user/show/91692751-cg">CG</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060526498" href="/book/show/18742.The_Melancholy_Death_of_Oyster_Boy_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3365016740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16707110961695641132">Tim Burton's artwork is often described as Goofy Gothic. Simple, surreal, and fantastically strange. I've always been a huge fan of Tim Burton's work in the past, (and ever since I was a kid.) So you can probably imagine how excited I was, to find out about the existence of this book. I recently got the chance to read it, and I'm happy to say that I wasn't disappointed. The poetry was bizarre and minimalistic, and the artwork simple and odd. (Each had that trademark Tim Burton style) that I love</span>
  <span id="freeText16707110961695641132" style="display:none">Tim Burton's artwork is often described as Goofy Gothic. Simple, surreal, and fantastically strange. I've always been a huge fan of Tim Burton's work in the past, (and ever since I was a kid.) So you can probably imagine how excited I was, to find out about the existence of this book. I recently got the chance to read it, and I'm happy to say that I wasn't disappointed. The poetry was bizarre and minimalistic, and the artwork simple and odd. (Each had that trademark Tim Burton style) that I loved.<br />I appreciated how it stayed fun and quick to read, and didn't necessarily have to be extremely complex, or wordy. (And some of the poems, were even pretty profound in thier simplicity, depending on how you viewed them.)<br />Examples like; Voodoo girl, Anchor baby, Mummy boy, and Junk girl. Etc.<br /><br />~Personal favorites/ones that stuck out to me~<br />-Mummy boy<br />-Anchor baby<br />-Voodoo girl<br />-James<br />-Junk girl<br />-Melonhead (aka me.)<br />-And Staring girl, (which fun fact: would later be the inspiration for the "Weird girl" character in Frankenweenie.)<br /><br /><br />Overall it was a short, entertaining and slightly gruesome, read.<br />4.5 stars ⭐⭐⭐⭐</span>

  <span id="freeText5814020124516463199" style="display:none">Truly entertaining! I started out reading to myself, however, I made a chortle and my hubby was curious, so, I began again at the beginning, this time, reading out loud. There seemed to be a similar theme to some of the stories, a longed-for offspring turning out to be something very different from imagined! Overall, an inventive and fun read with some surprises.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9988853377572184700">This book is full of mad ideas and sometimes disturbing themes, but overall these poems are easy to read, enjoyable and enhanced by the wonderful illustrations provided by Tim Burton. It is something that I could easily read just a few poems out of if I didn't have much time, or something that I will definitely be re-reading in its entirity at some point in the future. Robot Boy is my favourite of the collection due to the humour and interesting accompanying images.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2471040285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2471040285" />
    <a title="Paul Sánchez Keighley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25180638-paul-s-nchez-keighley"><img alt="Paul Sánchez Keighley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557221483p2/25180638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2471040285?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Sánchez Keighley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Sánchez Keighley" href="/user/show/25180638-paul-s-nchez-keighley">Paul Sánchez Keighley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25180638-paul-s-nchez-keighley?shelf=poesy">poesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25180638-paul-s-nchez-keighley?shelf=c-united-states">c-united-states</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2471040285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15705439120902507456"><i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton is exactly what you would expect from a book called <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton. I mean, come on, it's <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton! What were you expecting, Shakespeare's sonnets? If you were looking for Shakespeare's sonnets, why did you pick up a book called <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton? The rhymes aren't great, t</span>
  <span id="freeText15705439120902507456" style="display:none"><i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton is exactly what you would expect from a book called <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton. I mean, come on, it's <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton! What were you expecting, Shakespeare's sonnets? If you were looking for Shakespeare's sonnets, why did you pick up a book called <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton? The rhymes aren't great, the twists are morbid, the pictures are cute... Selfish parents give birth to freaks, said freaks struggle to fit in... Basically everything you would expect to find in a book called <i>The Melancholy Death of Oyster Boy and Other Stories</i> by Tim Burton. No more, no less.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15705439120902507456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GOf1o/LVvrcWw/8dPsdBzQ2AVWX6jU9lnHHnSlXmv6ntAEXpgDRWOVIrje0AiqZLTWuEcxfQ26x7SZB5HT8mcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8JE+Ucq1+rDN5TwYqY1EWLvcloez4h0gL5sX5UguO14Fdo4buFQSPokNTuiXwKPe+zdHkV6/ienIo2DWAPeihw==')})
  }

Gorey tells the tale of 26 children (each representing a letter of the alphabet) and their untimely deaths in rhyming dactylic couplets, accompanied by the author\'s distinctive black and white illustrations. It is one of Edward Gorey\'s best-known books, and is the most notorious amongst his roughly half-dozen mock alphabets.[2] It has been described as a &quot;sarcastic rebellion against a view of childhood that is sunny, idyllic, and instructive&quot;. The morbid humor of the book comes in part from the mundane ways in which children die, such as falling down the stairs or choking on a peach. Fruits was established in 1994, by photographer Shoich Aoki, initially as a project to document the growing explosion in street fashion within the suburbs of Tokyo. Your secret can be a regret, fear, betrayal, desire, confession, or childhood humiliation. Reveal anything -- as long as it is true and you have never shared it with anyone before. Be brief. Be legible. Be creative.\n\nIt all began with an idea Frank Warren had for a community art project. He began handing out postcards to strangers and leaving them in public places -- asking people to write down a secret they had never told anyone and mail it to him, anonymously.\n\nThe response was overwhelming. The secrets were both provocative and profound, and the cards themselves were works of art -- carefully and creatively constructed by hand. Addictively compelling, the cards reveal our deepest fears, desires, regrets, and obsessions. Frank calls them &quot;graphic haiku,&quot; beautiful, elegant, and small in structure but powerfully emotional.\n\nAs Frank began posting the cards on his website, PostSecret took on a life of its own, becoming much more than a simple art project. It has grown into a global phenomenon, exposing our individual aspirations, fantasies, and frailties -- our common humanity.\n\nEvery day dozens of postcards still make their way to Frank, with postmarks from around the world, touching on every aspect of human experience. This extraordinary collection brings together the most powerful, personal, and beautifully intimate secrets Frank Warren has received -- and brilliantly illuminates that human emotions can be unique
